queries is implemented through a multi-layered architecture that separates SQL code from parameters at every stage of query execution.\\n\\n## RawSQL Expression Sanitization\\n\\nThe **RawSQL** class (django/db/models/expressions.py:1236-1249) is the primary mechanism for safely writing raw SQL expressions. It requires developers to pass SQL and parameters separately: `RawSQL(sql, params, output_field=None)`. The params argument is mandatory and cannot be omitted, forcing developers to acknowledge they are using parameterization.\\n\\n## Raw QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe **QuerySet.raw()** method (django/db/models/query.py:1461-1473) accepts raw_query and params arguments separately. This method creates a RawQuerySet instance that passes both the SQL string and parameters through the execution pipeline without interpolating them together.\\n\\nThe **RawQuerySet** class (django/db/models/query.py:2285-2350) stores the raw SQL query and parameters separately, maintaining this separation throughout the object's lifetime.\\n\\n## Cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe critical execution point is in **RawQuery._execute_query()** (django/db/models/sql/query.py:208-225), which:\\n\\n1. Adapts parameters using `connection.ops.adapt_unknown_value()` to convert them to database-compatible types\\n2. Passes the SQL and adapted parameters separately to `cursor.execute(sql, params)` - never interpolating them together\\n3. Handles both tuple and dictionary parameter types (pyformat and named styles)\\n\\nThe **CursorWrapper** class (django/db/backends/utils.py:17-150) wraps all cursor execution through:\\n\\n- **execute()** method (lines 78-81): Routes to `_execute_with_wrappers()` with sql and params separated\\n- **executemany()** method (lines 83-86): Routes to `_execute_with_wrappers()` for batch execution\\n- **_execute()** method (lines 94-105): Calls underlying `cursor.execute(sql, params)` with separated parameters\\n- **_execute_with_wrappers()** method (lines 88-92): Allows execution wrappers while maintaining parameter separation\\n\\n## Backend-Specific Parameter Handling\\n\\nEach database backend implements parameter binding protection:\\n\\n**SQLite** (django/db/backends/sqlite3/base.py:340-379):\\n- **SQLiteCursorWrapper** converts Django's parameter styles (\\\"format\\\" and \\\"pyformat\\\") to SQLite's native styles (\\\"qmark\\\" and \\\"named\\\")\\n- **execute()** and **executemany()** methods (lines 353-370) perform parameter style conversion while maintaining separation\\n- **convert_query()** method (lines 372-378) safely transforms placeholders without interpolating parameters\\n\\n**PostgreSQL** (django/db/backends/postgresql/base.py:575-621):\\n- **ServerBindingCursor** enables server-side parameter binding when using psycopg3\\n- **Cursor** uses client-side parameter binding with psycopg3/psycopg2\\n- **ServerSideCursor** for named cursor support with client-side binding enforcement\\n\\n**Oracle** (django/db/backends/oracle/base.py):\\n- **OracleParam** class with **bind_parameter()** method handles late-binding cursor variables\\n- Parameters are wrapped in cursor variables before execution\\n\\n## Parameter Type Adaptation\\n\\nThe **BaseDatabaseOperations.adapt_unknown_value()** method (django/db/backends/base/operations.py:550-567) transforms Python values to database-compatible types:\\n\\n- Converts datetime.datetime to adapted datetime values\\n- Converts datetime.date to string representation\\n- Converts datetime.time to adapted time values  \\n- Converts decimal.Decimal to adapted decimal values\\n- Maintains type safety to prevent type-coercion attacks\\n\\n## Execution Wrapper System\\n\\nThe **CursorDebugWrapper** (django/db/backends/utils.py:117-150) wraps cursor execution for debugging while maintaining parameter separation through the `debug_sql()` context manager.\\n\\nAll execution goes through `_execute_with_wrappers()` which applies execute_wrappers while keeping sql and params separated throughout the call chain.\\n\\n## Documentation\\n\\nSQL injection protection is documented in:\\n- docs/topics/security.txt - SQL injection protection overview\\n- docs/topics/db/sql.txt - Raw query and parameter binding guidance\\n- docs/ref/models/expressions.txt - RawSQL expression requirements\\n\\nThe documentation emphasizes that params is a required argument and must not quote placeholders (e.g., avoid `RawSQL(\\\"WHERE col = '%s'\\\")` in favor of `RawSQL(\\\"WHERE col = queries is implemented through a multi-layered architecture that separates SQL code from parameters at every stage of query execution.\\n\\n## RawSQL Expression Sanitization\\n\\nThe **RawSQL** class (django/db/models/expressions.py:1236-1249) is the primary mechanism for safely writing raw SQL expressions. It requires developers to pass SQL and parameters separately: `RawSQL(sql, params, output_field=None)`. The params argument is mandatory and cannot be omitted, forcing developers to acknowledge they are using parameterization.\\n\\n## Raw QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe **QuerySet.raw()** method (django/db/models/query.py:1461-1473) accepts raw_query and params arguments separately. This method creates a RawQuerySet instance that passes both the SQL string and parameters through the execution pipeline without interpolating them together.\\n\\nThe **RawQuerySet** class (django/db/models/query.py:2285-2350) stores the raw SQL query and parameters separately, maintaining this separation throughout the object's lifetime.\\n\\n## Cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe critical execution point is in **RawQuery._execute_query()** (django/db/models/sql/query.py:208-225), which:\\n\\n1. Adapts parameters using `connection.ops.adapt_unknown_value()` to convert them to database-compatible types\\n2. Passes the SQL and adapted parameters separately to `cursor.execute(sql, params)` - never interpolating them together\\n3. Handles both tuple and dictionary parameter types (pyformat and named styles)\\n\\nThe **CursorWrapper** class (django/db/backends/utils.py:17-150) wraps all cursor execution through:\\n\\n- **execute()** method (lines 78-81): Routes to `_execute_with_wrappers()` with sql and params separated\\n- **executemany()** method (lines 83-86): Routes to `_execute_with_wrappers()` for batch execution\\n- **_execute()** method (lines 94-105): Calls underlying `cursor.execute(sql, params)` with separated parameters\\n- **_execute_with_wrappers()** method (lines 88-92): Allows execution wrappers while maintaining parameter separation\\n\\n## Backend-Specific Parameter Handling\\n\\nEach database backend implements parameter binding protection:\\n\\n**SQLite** (django/db/backends/sqlite3/base.py:340-379):\\n- **SQLiteCursorWrapper** converts Django's parameter styles (\\\"format\\\" and \\\"pyformat\\\") to SQLite's native styles (\\\"qmark\\\" and \\\"named\\\")\\n- **execute()** and **executemany()** methods (lines 353-370) perform parameter style conversion while maintaining separation\\n- **convert_query()** method (lines 372-378) safely transforms placeholders without interpolating parameters\\n\\n**PostgreSQL** (django/db/backends/postgresql/base.py:575-621):\\n- **ServerBindingCursor** enables server-side parameter binding when using psycopg3\\n- **Cursor** uses client-side parameter binding with psycopg3/psycopg2\\n- **ServerSideCursor** for named cursor support with client-side binding enforcement\\n\\n**Oracle** (django/db/backends/oracle/base.py):\\n- **OracleParam** class with **bind_parameter()** method handles late-binding cursor variables\\n- Parameters are wrapped in cursor variables before execution\\n\\n## Parameter Type Adaptation\\n\\nThe **BaseDatabaseOperations.adapt_unknown_value()** method (django/db/backends/base/operations.py:550-567) transforms Python values to database-compatible types:\\n\\n- Converts datetime.datetime to adapted datetime values\\n- Converts datetime.date to string representation\\n- Converts datetime.time to adapted time values  \\n- Converts decimal.Decimal to adapted decimal values\\n- Maintains type safety to prevent type-coercion attacks\\n\\n## Execution Wrapper System\\n\\nThe **CursorDebugWrapper** (django/db/backends/utils.py:117-150) wraps cursor execution for debugging while maintaining parameter separation through the `debug_sql()` context manager.\\n\\nAll execution goes through `_execute_with_wrappers()` which applies execute_wrappers while keeping sql and params separated throughout the call chain.\\n\\n## Documentation\\n\\nSQL injection protection is documented in:\\n- docs/topics/security.txt - SQL injection protection overview\\n- docs/topics/db/sql.txt - Raw query and parameter binding guidance\\n- docs/ref/models/expressions.txt - RawSQL expression requirements\\n\\nThe documentation emphasizes that params is a required argument and must not quote placeholders (e.g., avoid `RawSQL(\\\"WHERE col = '%s'\\\")` in favor of `RawSQL(\\\"WHERE col = %s\\\", [value])`)\\n\\n## Test Coverage\\n\\nSQL injection prevention is tested in tests/expressions/tests.py with `test_expressions_not_introduce_sql_injection_via_untrusted_string_inclusion()` demonstrating that malicious SQL injection attempts through expression filters are neutralized by parameter binding.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
